       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toyota_PRIUS_A_Premium_(DAA-ZVW51-AHXHB)_front_trimmed.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">
         Toyota Prius
        </a>
        is the world's top selling
        <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
         hybrid electric vehicle
        </a>
        , with global sales of 3.7 million units through April 2016.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PriusTop_1-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-PriusTop-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Some owners use its identity to make an environmental statement.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-2">
          [2]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>

     <div style="float:right">
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <b>
       green vehicle
      </b>
      or
      <b>
       environmentally-friendly vehicle
      </b>
      is a road
      <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">
       motor vehicle
      </a>
      that produces less harmful impacts to the
      <a href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">
       environment
      </a>
      than comparable conventional
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engine
      </a>
      vehicles running on
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">
       gasoline
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">
       diesel
      </a>
      , or one that uses certain
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_fuels" title="Alternative fuels">
       alternative fuels
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenStudent_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GreenStudent-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Presently, in some countries the term is used for any vehicle complying or surpassing the more stringent
      <a href="/wiki/European_emission_standards" title="European emission standards">
       European emission standards
      </a>
      (such as Euro6), or
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zero_emissions_vehicle" title="Zero emissions vehicle">
       zero emissions vehicle
      </a>
      standards (such as
      <a href="/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Zero-emissions vehicle">
       ZEV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ultra-low_emission_vehicle" title="Ultra-low emission vehicle">
       ULEV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Super_ultra-low_emission_vehicle" title="Super ultra-low emission vehicle">
       SULEV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Partial_zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Partial zero-emissions vehicle">
       PZEV
      </a>
      ), or the
      <a href="/wiki/Low-carbon_fuel_standard" title="Low-carbon fuel standard">
       low-carbon fuel standards
      </a>
      enacted in several countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Green vehicles can be powered by
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel" title="Alternative fuel">
       alternative fuels
      </a>
      and advanced vehicle technologies and include
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       hybrid electric vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid electric vehicle">
       plug-in hybrid electric vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">
       battery electric vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed-air_vehicle" title="Compressed-air vehicle">
       compressed-air vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle" title="Hydrogen vehicle">
       hydrogen
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel-cell_vehicle" title="Fuel-cell vehicle">
       fuel-cell vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neat_ethanol_vehicle" title="Neat ethanol vehicle">
       neat ethanol vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">
       flexible-fuel vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">
       natural gas vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clean_diesel" title="Clean diesel">
       clean diesel
      </a>
      vehicles, and some sources also include vehicles using blends of
      <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">
       biodiesel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">
       ethanol fuel
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gasohol" title="Gasohol">
       gasohol
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenStudent_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-GreenStudent-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several author also include conventional motor vehicles with high
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">
       fuel economy
      </a>
      , as they consider that increasing fuel economy is the most
      <a href="/wiki/Cost-effectiveness_analysis" title="Cost-effectiveness analysis">
       cost-effective
      </a>
      way to improve energy efficiency and reduce carbon emissions in the transport sector in the short run.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As part of their contribution to
      <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_transport" title="Sustainable transport">
       sustainable transport
      </a>
      , these vehicles reduce
      <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">
       air pollution
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emission" title="Greenhouse gas emission">
       greenhouse gas emissions
      </a>
      , and contribute to
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">
       energy independence
      </a>
      by reducing oil imports.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenStudent_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-GreenStudent-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TwoBillion_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-TwoBillion-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      An environmental analysis extends beyond just the operating efficiency and emissions. A
      <a href="/wiki/Life-cycle_assessment" title="Life-cycle assessment">
       life-cycle assessment
      </a>
      involves production and post-use considerations. A
      <a href="/wiki/Cradle-to-cradle_design" title="Cradle-to-cradle design">
       cradle-to-cradle design
      </a>
      is more important than a focus on a single factor such as energy efficiency.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_efficiency">
       Energy efficiency
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Energy efficiency">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Cars with similar production of energy costs can obtain, during the life of the car (operational phase), large reductions in energy costs through several measures:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The most significant is by using
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_propulsion" title="Alternative propulsion">
        alternative propulsion
       </a>
       :
       <ul>
        <li>
         An efficient engine that reduces the vehicle's consumption of
         <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
          petroleum
         </a>
         (i.e.
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petroleum_electric_hybrid_vehicle" title="Petroleum electric hybrid vehicle">
          petroleum electric hybrid vehicle
         </a>
         ), or that uses
         <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
          renewable energy
         </a>
         sources throughout its working life.
        </li>
        <li>
         Using
         <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">
          biofuels
         </a>
         instead of petroleum fuels.
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
      <li>
       Proper maintenance of a vehicle such as engine
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tune-up" title="wikt:tune-up">
        tune-ups
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_change" title="Oil change">
        oil changes
       </a>
       , and maintaining proper
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tire_pressure" title="Tire pressure">
        tire pressure
       </a>
       can also help.
      </li>
      <li>
       Removing unnecessary items from a vehicle reduces weight and improves fuel economy as well.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto">
      <tr>
       <th colspan="6" style="text-align:center; background:#cfc;">
        Comparison of several types of green car basic characteristics
        <br/>

         Fuel economy
        </a>
        <br/>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miles_per_gallon" title="Miles per gallon">
         mpg
        </a>
        equivalent)
       </td>
       <td style="text-align:center; background:#cfc;">

        Payback period
       </td>
      </tr>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Types">
       Types
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="738" data-file-width="1506" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png/400px-Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png/600px-Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png/800px-Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png 2x" width="400"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battery_EV_vs._Hydrogen_EV.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Comparison of energy efficiency between
        <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">
         battery
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle" title="Hydrogen vehicle">
         hydrogen
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel-cell" title="Fuel-cell">
         fuel-cell
        </a>
        cars.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="897" data-file-width="1705" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG/220px-Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG/330px-Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG/440px-Chevrolet_Volt_WAS_2011_837.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="1125" data-file-width="1946" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg/220px-2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg/330px-2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg/440px-2011_Nissan_Leaf_--_2011_DC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Sales of both the
         <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">
          Chevrolet Volt
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
          plug-in hybrid
         </a>
         (top) and the
         <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">
          Nissan Leaf
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-electric_car" title="All-electric car">
          all-electric car
         </a>
         (bottom) began in December 2010.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG/220px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG/330px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG/440px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_8120.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        PSA Peugeot Citroën Hybrid Air concept exhibited at the 2013
        <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">
         Geneva Motor Show
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">
       Alternative fuel vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Green vehicles include vehicles types that function fully or partly on alternative energy sources other than
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
       fossil fuel
      </a>
      or less carbon intensive than gasoline or diesel.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another option is the use of
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel" title="Alternative fuel">
       alternative fuel
      </a>
      composition in conventional fossil fuel-based vehicles, making them function partially on renewable energy sources. Other approaches include
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">
       personal rapid transit
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">
       public transportation
      </a>
      concept that offers automated, on-demand, non-stop transportation on a network of specially built guideways.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_and_fuel_cell-powered">
       Electric and fuel cell-powered
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Electric and fuel cell-powered">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">
       Electric vehicle
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       Plug-in hybrid
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Examples of vehicles with reduced petroleum consumption include
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       plug-in hybrids
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">
       fuel cell
      </a>
      -powered
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrogen_car" title="Hydrogen car">
       hydrogen cars
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       Electric cars
      </a>
      are typically more efficient than
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">
       fuel cell
      </a>
      -powered vehicles on a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank-to-wheel" title="Tank-to-wheel">
       Tank-to-wheel
      </a>
      basis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      For this reason
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">
       battery powered vehicles
      </a>
      and plug-in hybrids are gaining popularity. They have better
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">
       fuel economy
      </a>
      than conventional
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engine
      </a>
      vehicles but are hampered by
      <a href="/wiki/All-electric_range" title="All-electric range">
       range
      </a>
      or maximum distance attainable before discharging the battery. The
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car#Batteries" title="Electric car">
       electric car batteries
      </a>
      are their main cost. They provide a 0%
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      to 99.9% reduction in
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">
       CO
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
      </a>
      emissions compared to an
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       ICE
      </a>
      (gasoline, diesel) vehicle, depending on the source of electricity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_electric_vehicles">
       Hybrid electric vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hybrid electric vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">
       Hybrid vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_car" title="Hybrid car">
       Hybrid cars
      </a>
      may be partly fossil fuel (or biofuel) powered and partly electric or hydrogen-powered. Most combine an internal combustion engine with an electric engine, though other variations too exist. The internal combustion engine is often either a gasoline or Diesel engine (in rare cases a Stirling engine may even be used
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      ). They are more expensive to purchase but cost redemption is achieved in a period of about 5 years due to better fuel economy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Compressed_air_cars.2C_stirling_vehicles.2C_and_others">
       Compressed air cars, stirling vehicles, and others
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Compressed air cars, stirling vehicles, and others">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed-air_vehicle" title="Compressed-air vehicle">
       Compressed-air vehicle
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air_car" title="Compressed air car">
       Compressed air car
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air_car" title="Compressed air car">
       Compressed air cars
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Zero-emissions vehicle">
       stirling-powered
      </a>
      vehicles,
      <a href="/wiki/Liquid_nitrogen_vehicle" title="Liquid nitrogen vehicle">
       Liquid nitrogen vehicles
      </a>
      are even less polluting than electrical vehicles, as the vehicle and its components can be made more environmentally friendly.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Solar_car_racing" title="Solar car racing">
       Solar car races
      </a>
      are held on a regular basis in order to promote green vehicles and other "
      <a href="/wiki/Environmental_technology" title="Environmental technology">
       green technology
      </a>
      ". These sleek driver-only vehicles can travel long distances at highway speeds using only the electricity generated instantaneously from the sun.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Improving_conventional_cars">
       Improving conventional cars
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Improving conventional cars">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1291" data-file-width="1877" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg/220px-Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg/330px-Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg/440px-Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brazilian_Fiat_Siena_TetraFuel_four_views.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Siena" title="Fiat Siena">
         Fiat Siena Tetrafuel
        </a>
        1.4 is a
        <a href="/wiki/Multifuel" title="Multifuel">
         multifuel
        </a>
        car designed to run as a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flex-fuel" title="Flex-fuel">
         flex-fuel
        </a>
        on
        <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">
         gasoline
        </a>
        , or
        <a href="/wiki/Common_ethanol_fuel_mixtures#E20.2C_E25" title="Common ethanol fuel mixtures">
         E20-E25 blend
        </a>
        , or neat ethanol (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neat_alcohol_fuel" title="Neat alcohol fuel">
         E100
        </a>
        ); or to run as a
        <a href="/wiki/Bi-fuel_vehicle" title="Bi-fuel vehicle">
         bi-fuel
        </a>
        with
        <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">
         natural gas (CNG)
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">
       Biofuel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">
       compressed natural gas
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clean_diesel" title="Clean diesel">
       clean diesel
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_emissions_scandal" title="Volkswagen emissions scandal">
       Volkswagen emissions scandal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A conventional vehicle can become a greener vehicle by mixing in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_fuel" title="Renewable fuel">
       renewable fuels
      </a>
      or using less carbon intensive
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
       fossil fuel
      </a>
      . Typical
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">
       gasoline
      </a>
      -powered cars can tolerate up to 10%
      <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_fuel" title="Alcohol fuel">
       ethanol
      </a>
      . Brazil manufactured cars that run on neat ethanol, though there were discontinued. Another available option is a
      <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">
       flexible-fuel vehicle
      </a>
      which allows any blend of gasoline and ethanol, up to 85% in North America and Europe, and up to 100% in Brazil.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another existing option is to convert a conventional gasoline-powered to allow the alternative use of
      <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">
       CNG
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">
       Pakistan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
       Argentina
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Iran
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       India
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italy
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      have the largest fleets of
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">
       natural gas vehicles
      </a>
      in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IANGV_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IANGV-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">
       Diesel
      </a>
      -powered vehicles can often transition completely to
      <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">
       biodiesel
      </a>
      , though the fuel is a very strong
      <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">
       solvent
      </a>
      , which can occasionally damage
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber">
       rubber
      </a>
      seals in vehicles built before 1994. More commonly, however, biodiesel causes problems simply because it removes all of the built-up residue in an engine, clogging
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filter_(chemistry)" title="Filter (chemistry)">
       filters
      </a>
      , unless care is taken when switching from dirty fossil-fuel derived diesel to bio-diesel. It is very effective at 'de-coking' the diesel engines combustion chambers and keeping them clean. Biodiesel is the lowest emission fuel available for diesel engines. Diesel engines are the most efficient car internal combustion engines. Biodiesel is the only fuel allowed in some North American national parks because spillages will completely bio-degrade within 21 days. Biodiesel and
      <a href="/wiki/Vegetable_oil_fuel" title="Vegetable oil fuel">
       vegetable oil fuelled
      </a>
      , diesel engined vehicles have been declared amongst the greenest in the US
      <i>
       Tour de Sol
      </i>
      competition.
     </p>
     <p>
      This presents problems, as biofuels can use food resources in order to provide mechanical energy for vehicles. Many experts point to this as a reason for growing food prices, particularly US Bio-ethanol fuel production which has affected maize prices. In order to have a low environmental impact, biofuels should be made only from waste products, or from new sources like
      <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">
       algae
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_Motor_and_Pedal_Powered_Vehicles">
       Electric Motor and Pedal Powered Vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Electric Motor and Pedal Powered Vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Multiple companies are offering and developing two, three, and four wheel vehicles combining the characteristics of a bicycle with electric motors. US Federal, State and Local laws do not clearly nor consistently classify
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      these vehicles as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycles" title="Bicycles">
       bicycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_bicycles" title="Electric bicycles">
       electric bicycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorcycles" title="Motorcycles">
       motorcycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles" title="Electric motorcycles">
       electric motorcycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mopeds" title="Mopeds">
       mopeds
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood_Electric_Vehicle" title="Neighborhood Electric Vehicle">
       Neighborhood Electric Vehicle
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Motorised_quadricycle" title="Motorised quadricycle">
       motorised quadricycle
      </a>
      or as a
      <a href="/wiki/Car" title="Car">
       car
      </a>
      . Some laws have limits on top speeds, power of the motors, range, etc. while others do not.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
       Other
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">
       Personal rapid transit
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Borealis3windmills.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1193" data-file-width="2000" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Borealis3windmills.jpg/220px-Borealis3windmills.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Borealis3windmills.jpg/330px-Borealis3windmills.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Borealis3windmills.jpg/440px-Borealis3windmills.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Borealis3windmills.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">
         Solar vehicle
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transportation" title="Public transportation">
        Public transportation
       </a>
       vehicles are not usually included in the green vehicle category, but
       <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">
        Personal rapid transit
       </a>
       (PRT) vehicles probably should be. All vehicles that are powered from the track have the advantage of potentially being able to use any source of electric energy, including sustainable ones, rather than requiring liquid fuels. They can also switch regenerative braking energy between vehicles and the electric grid rather than requiring energy storage on the vehicles. Also, they can potentially use the entire track area for solar collectors, not just the vehicle surface. The potential
       <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit#Energy_efficiency" title="Personal rapid transit">
        PRT energy efficiency
       </a>
       is much higher than that which traditional automobiles can attain.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">
        Solar vehicles
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">
        electric vehicles
       </a>
       powered by
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">
        solar energy
       </a>
       obtained from
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">
        solar panels
       </a>
       on the surface (generally, the roof) of the vehicle.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" title="Photovoltaic">
        Photovoltaic
       </a>
       (PV) cells convert the Sun's energy directly into
       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_energy" title="Electrical energy">
        electrical energy
       </a>
       . Solar vehicles are not practical day-to-day transportation devices at present, but are primarily demonstration vehicles and engineering exercises, often sponsored by government agencies. However, some cities have begun offering
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_bus" title="Solar bus">
        solar-powered buses
       </a>
       , including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tindo" title="Tindo">
        Tindo
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">
        Adelaide, Australia
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind-powered_land_vehicle" title="Wind-powered land vehicle">
        Wind-powered electric vehicles
       </a>
       primarily use wind-turbines installed at a strategic point of the vehicle, which are then converted into electric energy which causes the vehicle to propel.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_powered_vehicles">
       Animal powered vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Animal powered vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horse_and_carriage" title="Horse and carriage">
       Horse and carriage
      </a>
      are just one type of animal propelled vehicle. Once a common form of transportation, they became far less common as cities grew and automobiles took their place. In dense cities, the waste produced by large numbers of transportation animals was a significant health problem. Oftentimes the food is produced for them using diesel powered tractors, and thus there is some environmental impact as a result of their use.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_powered_vehicles">
       Human powered vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Human powered vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg/220px-V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg/330px-V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg/440px-V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:V%C3%A9lo%27v_station_5002_-_Place_des_Compagnons_de_la_chanson.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9lo%27v" title="Vélo'v">
         Vélo'v
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" title="Bicycle sharing system">
         bicycle sharing system
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">
         Lyon
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
         France
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" title="Bicycle sharing system">
       Bicycle sharing system
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Human powered transport includes walking,
      <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">
       bicycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Velomobile" title="Velomobile">
       velomobiles
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Row_boat" title="Row boat">
       row boats
      </a>
      , and other environmentally friendly ways of getting around. In addition to the health benefits of the exercise provided, they are far more environmentally friendly than most other options. The only downside is the speed limitations, and how far one can travel before getting exhausted.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Benefits_of_green_vehicle_use">
       Benefits of green vehicle use
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Benefits of green vehicle use">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">
       Environmental
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Environmental">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Vehicle emissions contribute to the increasing concentration of gases linked to
      <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">
       climate change
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-world_energy_council_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-world_energy_council-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In order of significance, the principal
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" title="Greenhouse gases">
       greenhouse gases
      </a>
      associated with road transport are carbon dioxide (CO
      <sub>
       2
      </sub>
      ), methane (CH
      <sub>
       4
      </sub>
      ) and nitrous oxide (N
      <sub>
       2
      </sub>
      O).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Road transport is the third largest source of greenhouse gases emitted in the UK, and accounts for over 20% of total emissions,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 33% in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of the total greenhouse gas emissions from transport, over 85% are due to CO
      <sub>
       2
      </sub>
      emissions from road vehicles. The transport sector is the fastest growing source of greenhouse gases.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPCC_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IPCC-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
       Health
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Health">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Vehicle pollutants have been linked to human ill health including the incidence of respiratory and cardiopulmonary disease and lung cancer. A 1998 report estimated that up to 24,000 people die prematurely each year in the UK as a direct result of air pollution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Health_Organisation" title="World Health Organisation">
       World Health Organisation
      </a>
      , up to 13,000 deaths per year among children (aged 0–4 years) across Europe are directly attributable to outdoor pollution. The organization estimates that if pollution levels were returned to within EU limits, more than 5,000 of these lives could be saved each year.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Monetary">
       Monetary
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Monetary">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_taxi" title="Hybrid taxi">
       Hybrid taxi
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fleet_operator" title="Fleet operator">
       fleet operators
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York
      </a>
      have also reported that reduced fuel consumption saves them thousands of dollars per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">
       Criticism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Criticism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A study by CNW Marketing Research suggested that the extra energy cost of manufacture, shipping, disposal, and the short lives of some of these types of vehicle (particularly gas-electric
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">
       hybrid vehicles
      </a>
      ) outweighs any energy savings made by their using less petroleum during their useful lifespan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This type of argument is the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Long_smokestack&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Long smokestack (page does not exist)">
       long smokestack
      </a>
      argument.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Critics of the report note that the study prorated all of Toyota's hybrid research-and-development costs across the relatively small number of Priuses on the road, rather than using the incremental cost of building a vehicle; used109,000 miles (175,000 km) for the length of life of a Prius (Toyota offers a 150,000-mile (240,000 km) warranty on the Prius' hybrid components, including the battery), and calculated that a majority of a car's cradle-to-grave energy gets expended during the vehicle's production, not while it is driven.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Consumer_Ombudsman" title="Norwegian Consumer Ombudsman">
       Norwegian Consumer Ombudsman
      </a>
      official Bente Øverli stated that "Cars cannot do anything good for the environment except less damage than others." Based on this opinion, Norwegian law severely restricts the use of "
      <a href="/wiki/Greenwashing" title="Greenwashing">
       greenwashing
      </a>
      " to market automobiles, strongly prohibiting advertising a vehicle as being environmentally friendly, with large fines issued to violators.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A study that looked at other factors other than energy consumption and carbon emissions has suggested that there is no such thing as an environmentally friendly car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The use of vehicles with increased fuel efficiency is usually considered positive in the short term but criticism of any hydrocarbon-based personal transport remains. The
      <a href="/wiki/Jevons_paradox" title="Jevons paradox">
       Jevons paradox
      </a>
      suggests that energy efficiency programs are often counter-productive, even increasing energy consumption in the long run.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many environmental researchers believe that
      <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_transport" title="Sustainable transport">
       sustainable transport
      </a>
      may require a move away from hydrocarbon fuels and from our present automobile and highway paradigm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="National_and_international_promotion">
       National and international promotion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: National and international promotion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">
       European Union
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: European Union">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      is promoting the marketing of greener cars via a combination of binding and non-binding measures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of April 2010, 15 of the 27
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" title="Member states of the European Union">
       member states of the European Union
      </a>
      provide tax incentives for
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">
       electrically chargeable vehicles
      </a>
      and some
      <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">
       alternative fuel vehicles
      </a>
      , which includes all
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
       Western European
      </a>
      countries except
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italy
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">
       Luxembourg
      </a>
      , plus the
      <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
       Czech Republic
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
       Romania
      </a>
      . The incentives consist of tax reductions and exemptions, as well as of bonus payments for buyers of
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       plug-in hybrids
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       hybrid electric vehicles
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">
       natural gas vehicles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GCC0420_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GCC0420-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACEA2_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ACEA2-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
       United States
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: United States">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">
       United States Environmental Protection Agency
      </a>
      (EPA) is promoting the marketing of greener cars via the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SmartWay" title="SmartWay">
       SmartWay
      </a>
      program. The SmartWay and SmartWay Elite designation mean that a vehicle is a better environmental performer relative to other vehicles. This US EPA designation is arrived at by taking into account a vehicle's Air Pollution Score and Greenhouse Gas Score. Higher Air Pollution Scores indicate vehicles that emit lower amounts of pollutants that cause smog relative to other vehicles. Higher Greenhouse Gas Scores indicate vehicles that emit lower amounts of carbon dioxide and have improved fuel economy relative to other vehicles.
     </p>
     <p>
      To earn the SmartWay designation, a vehicle must earn at least a 6 on the Air Pollution Score and at least a 6 on the Greenhouse Gas Score, but have a combined score of at least 13. SmartWay Elite is given to those vehicles that score 9 or better on both the Greenhouse Gas and Air Pollution Scores.
     </p>
     <p>
      A Green Vehicle Marketing Alliance, in conjunction with the
      <a href="/wiki/Oak_Ridge_National_Laboratory" title="Oak Ridge National Laboratory">
       Oak Ridge National Laboratory
      </a>
      (ONRL), periodically meets, and coordinates marketing efforts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Progressive_Insurance_Automotive_X_Prize">
       Progressive Insurance Automotive X Prize
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Progressive Insurance Automotive X Prize">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The Progressive Insurance Automotive X PRIZE (PIAXP) is a set of competitions, programs and events, from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X_PRIZE_Foundation" title="X PRIZE Foundation">
       X PRIZE Foundation
      </a>
      to "inspire a new generation of super-efficient vehicles that help break America's addiction to oil and stem the effects of climate change."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Corporation" title="Progressive Corporation">
       Progressive Insurance
      </a>
      is the title sponsor of the prize, the centerpiece of which is the Competition Division, within which a $10 million purse will be divided between the winners of three competitions.
     </p>
     <p>
      The essence of each competition is to design, build and race super-efficient vehicles that will achieve 100
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miles_per_gallon_of_gasoline_equivalent" title="Miles per gallon of gasoline equivalent">
       MPGe
      </a>
      (2.35 liter/100 kilometer) and can be produced for the mass market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Within the Competition Division, there are two vehicle classes: Mainstream and Alternative. The mainstream class has a prize of $5 million. The alternate class has 2 separate prizes of $2.5 million, one for side-by-side seating and one for tandem seating.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guidelines_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-guidelines-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some of the competitors, such as Aptera and Tesla, are already taking deposits for 'green' vehicles from customers.
     </p>

     <p>
      Several automobile magazines, motor vehicle specialized publications and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_group" title="Environmental group">
       environmental groups
      </a>
      publish annual rankings or listings of the best green
      <a href="/wiki/Car_of_the_Year" title="Car of the Year">
       cars of a given year
      </a>
      . The following table presents a selection of the annual top pickings.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Green_vehicle_motor_shows">
       Green vehicle motor shows
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Green vehicle motor shows">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_show" title="Motor show">
       Motor show
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Dedicated
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">
       electric
      </a>
      and green vehicle motor shows:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Alternative Vehicle and Fuel Show (AVFS),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_of_Valladolid" title="Fair of Valladolid">
        Fair of Valladolid
       </a>
       , Spain, in November.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Green Fleet Expo,
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Gardens_(Ontario)" title="Royal Botanical Gardens (Ontario)">
        Royal Botanical Gardens (Ontario)
       </a>
       , in May.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Green-Car-Guide Live!,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arena_and_Convention_Centre" title="Arena and Convention Centre">
        Arena and Convention Centre
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">
        Liverpool
       </a>
       , in June
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Electric_Motor_Show" title="European Electric Motor Show">
        European Electric Motor Show
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helsinki_Exhibition_%26_Convention_Centre" title="Helsinki Exhibition &amp; Convention Centre">
        Helsinki Exhibition &amp; Convention Centre
       </a>
       , in November
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>

          </sup>

         <cite class="citation news">
          Voelcker, John (2015-12-21).
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.greencarreports.com/news/1101506_2016-toyota-prius-most-fuel-efficient-car-without-a-plug-ever" rel="nofollow">
           "2016 Toyota Prius: Most Fuel-Efficient Car Without A Plug, Ever"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Green Car Reports
          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2015-12-26
           </span>
          </span>
          .
         </cite>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGreen+vehicle&amp;rft.atitle=2016+Toyota+Prius%3A+Most+Fuel-Efficient+Car+Without+A+Plug%2C+Ever&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.aulast=Voelcker&amp;rft.date=2015-12-21&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.greencarreports.com%2Fnews%2F1101506_2016-toyota-prius-most-fuel-efficient-car-without-a-plug-ever&amp;rft.jtitle=Green+Car+Reports&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         The first generation
         <a href="/wiki/Honda_Insight" title="Honda Insight">
          Honda Insight
         </a>
         was the most fuel efficient gasoline-powered car available in the U.S. without
         <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">
          plug-in capability
         </a>
         for the length of its production run and until December 2015, when it was surpassed by the 2016
         <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius#Fourth_generation_.282015.E2.80.93present.29" title="Toyota Prius">
          Toyota Prius Eco
         </a>
         .
        </span>
       </li>
